Note that
\[\frac{a^2 + b^2}{a - b} = a + b + \frac{2b^2}{a - b}.\]From $ab = 8,$ $b = \frac{8}{a},$ so
\[\frac{a^2 + b^2}{a - b} = a + b + \frac{16}{a^2 - 8/a}.\]Let $t = a - \frac{4}{a}.$  Then
\begin{align*}
\frac{a^2 + b^2}{a - b} &= \left( t + \frac{4}{a} \right) + \left( t + \frac{4}{a^2} \right) + \frac{16}{t} \\
&= t + \frac{4}{a} + \frac{4}{a^2} + t + \frac{16}{t} \\
&= 2t + \frac{4}{a} + \frac{4}{a^2} + \frac{16}{t}.
\end{align*}Since $a > b = \frac{8}{a},$ $a^2 > 8,$ so $t = a - \frac{4}{a} > 0.$

By AM-GM,
\[2t + 8 \ge 2 \sqrt{(2t)(8)} = 4 \sqrt{2t}.\]Also, by AM-GM,
\[\frac{4}{a} + \frac{4}{a^2} \ge 2 \sqrt{\frac{16}{a^3}} = \frac{8}{\sqrt{a^3}}.\]Finally, by AM-GM,
\[\frac{16}{t} \ge 8 \sqrt{\frac{2}{t}}.\]Multiplying all these inequalities, we get
\[2t + \frac{4}{a} + \frac{4}{a^2} + \frac{16}{t} \ge 4 \sqrt{2t} \cdot \frac{8}{\sqrt{a^3}} \cdot 8 \sqrt{\frac{2}{t}} = \frac{256}{\sqrt{a^3}},\]so
\[\frac{a^2 + b^2}{a - b} \ge \frac{256}{\sqrt{a^3}}.\]We want to minimize $\frac{a^2 + b^2}{a - b},$ so we want to maximize $\sqrt{a^3}.$  Since $ab = 8,$ $a^2 = \frac{8}{b}.$  Then
\[\sqrt{a^3} = a \sqrt{a} = \sqrt{8b} \cdot \sqrt{\frac{8}{b}} = 8.\]Therefore, the minimum of $\frac{a^2 + b^2}{a - b}$ is $\boxed{32}.$  Equality occurs when $a = 2 \sqrt{2} + \sqrt{6}$ and $b = 2 \sqrt{2} - \sqrt{6}.$

Since $f$ has rational coefficients, $1-2\sqrt{3}$ is also a root. Also, $3+\sqrt{2}$ must be a root as well, since the coefficients of $f$ are rational. Now, note that $1+2\sqrt{3}$ and $1-2\sqrt{3}$ are conjugates, and likewise, $3+\sqrt{2}$ and $3-\sqrt{2}$ are conjugates. Therefore, their product are differences of squares with rational coefficients, which means that they are rational:
\begin{align*}
(1+2\sqrt{3})(1-2\sqrt{3}) &= 1 - (2\sqrt{3})^2 = -5, \\
(3+\sqrt{2})(3-\sqrt{2}) &= 3^2 - (\sqrt{2})^2 = 7.
\end{align*}
Thus $f$ factors as \[f(x) = a(x-1-2\sqrt{3})(x-1+2\sqrt{3})(x-3+\sqrt{2})(x-3-\sqrt{2})\]for some nonzero rational number $a.$ The leading coefficient is $a$ times the product of the roots, hence $a = \frac{-154}{(2\sqrt{3}+2\sqrt{2})(2\sqrt{3}-2\sqrt{2})}= -7.$ Therefore, \[f(x) = -7(x-1-2\sqrt{3})(x-1+2\sqrt{3})(x-3+\sqrt{2})(x-3-\sqrt{2}).\]Let $x = 1.$ Then $f(1) = -7(-1-2\sqrt{3})(-1+2\sqrt{3})(-2+\sqrt{2})(-2-\sqrt{2}).$ Noting that $(-1-2\sqrt{3})(-1+2\sqrt{3}) = -10$ and $(-2+\sqrt{2})(-2-\sqrt{2}) = -6,$ we have \[f(1) = -7 \cdot (-10)(-6) = \boxed{-420}.\]

By Cauchy-Schwarz,
\[(3^2 + 4^2)(b^2 + c^2) \ge (3b + 4c)^2.\]Since $a + 3b + 4c = a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 25,$ we can write this as
\[25(25 - a^2) \ge (25 - a)^2.\]Expanding, we get
\[625 - 25a^2 \ge 625 - 50a + a^2,\]so $26a^2 - 50a \le 0.$  This factors as $2a(13a - 25) \le 0.$  This implies $a \le \frac{25}{13}.$

Square the equation $a + 3b + 4c = 25,$ to get
\[a^2 + 6ab + 8ac + 9b^2 + 24bc + 16c^2 = 625.\]Then $a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 25,$ so $b^2 + 6ab + 8ac + 24bc + 15c^2 = 600.$  Then
\[c(8a + 24b + 30c) = 600 - b^2 - 6ab - 15c^2.\]Also, $a^2 = 25 - b^2 - c^2,$ so we can substitute:
\[c(8a + 24b + 30c) = 50a - 175.\]Since $8a + 24b + 30c > 0,$

Extracting Answer from: 
We wish to divide $x^{100}$ by $x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1,$ but we have no nice way to divide. Instead we turn to the Factor Theorem: if $f(a) = 0,$ then $x - a$ is a factor of $f(x).$

If $\omega$ is one of the roots of $x^5 = 1,$ then
\[(x - \omega)(x - \omega^2)(x - \omega^3)(x - \omega^4)\]is a divisor of $x^5 - 1.$ This polynomial factors as
\[x^5 - 1 = (x - 1)(x^4 + x^3 + x^2 + x + 1).\]Thus the four factors above are divisors of $x^4 + x^3 + x^2 + X + 1.$

If $\omega$ is a root of $x^5 = 1,$ then
\begin{align*}
(\omega^3)^2 &= \omega^6 = \omega \\
(\omega^3)^3 &= \omega^9 = \omega^4 \\
(\omega^3)^4 &= \omega^{12} = \omega^2 \\
(\omega^3)^5 &= \omega^{15} = \omega^3
\end{align*}so $\omega^3$ is a primitive fifth root of unity. Hence,
\begin{align*}
\omega^3 + 1 &= \frac{\omega^6 - 1}{\omega^3 - 1} + 1 \\
&= \frac{\omega^3 + 1}{\omega^3 - 1}.
\end{align*}Then $(\omega^3 + 1)(\omega^3 - 1) = \omega^6 - 1,$ so
\begin{align*}
\omega^4 + \omega^3 + \omega^2 + \omega + 1 &= \frac{\omega^4(\omega^4 + \omega^3 + \omega^2 + \omega + 1)}{\omega^4} \\
&= \frac{\omega^4 - 1}{\omega^3 - 1} \\
&= \omega + \omega^4(\omega^3 - 1)^{-1} \\
&= \omega + \omega^4 \omega^{-3} \\
&= \omega^2 - \omega + 1,
\end{align*}since $\omega^5 = 1.$ We have shown that
\[x^4 + x^3 + x^2 + x + 1 = (x^2 - x + 1)(x^2 + x + 1).\]Thus,
\[x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1 = (x^4 + x^3 + x^2 + x + 1)(x^4 - x^3 + x^2 - x + 1).\]Any root of $x^4 + x^3 + x^2 + x + 1$ is a fifth root of unity, or the reciprocal of a fifth root of unity, so
\[x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1 = \prod_{n = 1}^8 \left( x - \omega^n \right)\]and
\[x^{100} = (x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1) Q(x) + R(x)\]for some polynomial $Q(x)$ and some polynomial $R(x)$ with degree less than 8. Since $\deg R(x) < 8,$
\[R(x) = a_0 + a_1 x + a_2 x^2 + \dots + a_7 x^7\]for some coefficients $a_0,$ $a_1,$ $\dots,$ $a_7.$

Setting $x = \omega,$  $\omega^2,$ $\omega^3,$ $\dots,$ $\omega^8,$ we find that
\[R(\omega) = R(\omega^2) = R(\omega^3) = R(\omega^4) = R(\omega^5) = 0.\]On the other hand, $R(1) = 1.$ Hence,
\[R(x) = (x - \omega)(x - \omega^2)(x - \omega^3)(x - \omega^4)(x - \omega^5) = (x^2 + x + 1)(x^2 - x + 1)(x^4 + x^3 + x^2 + x + 1),\]so the remainder when $x^{100}$ is divided by $x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1$ is $\boxed{x^7 + x^2 + 1}.$

Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.

From the equation $\left| \frac{z - 4}{z - 8} \right| = 1,$ $|z - 4| = |z - 8|.$  Then
\[|x + yi - 4| = |x + yi - 8|,\]so $(x - 4)^2 + y^2 = (x - 8)^2 + y^2.$  This simplifies to $x = 6.$

From the equation $\left| \frac{z - 12}{z - 8i} \right| = \frac{5}{3},$ $3|z - 12| = 5|z - 8i|.$  Then
\[3|6 + yi - 12| = 5|6 + yi - 8i|,\]so $9(36 + y^2) = 25(36 + (y - 8)^2).$  This simplifies to $16y^2 - 400y + 2176 = 0,$ which factors as $16(y - 8)(y - 17) = 0.$  Hence, $y = 8$ or $y = 17.$

Thus, the solutions in $z$ are $\boxed{6 + 8i, 6 + 17i}.$

First we analyze the equation $|z-4|=|z-8|$. Consider the complex plane, and let $O$ be the origin, $A$ correspond to $z=4$, and $B$ correspond to $z=8$. Then $|z-4|$ is the distance from $A$ to $z$, and $|z-8|$ is the distance from $B$ to $z$. Therefore, the equation $|z-4|=|z-8|$ tells us that $z$ must lie on the perpendicular bisector of segment $AB$. Since $OAB$ is a right triangle, the perpendicular bisector of side $AB$ is just the altitude from the right angle, which passes through the midpoint $C$ of hypotenuse $OB$. Since $O=(0,0)$, $A=(4,0)$, and $B=(8,0)$ are collinear on the $x$-axis, the midpoint is $C = (\tfrac{1}{2}(0+8),\tfrac{1}{2}(0+0)) = (4,0)$. Therefore, all complex numbers $z$ that satisfy $|z-4|=|z-8|$ must lie on the line $x=4$.

Now we analyze the equation $|z-12|=\tfrac{5}{3}|z-8i|$. Let $D$ be the point corresponding to $z=12$, and let $E$ be the point corresponding to $z=8i$. Then we have $|z-12|$ is the distance from $D$ to $z$, and $\tfrac{5}{3}|z-8i|$ is $\tfrac{5}{3}$ times the distance from $E$ to $z$. Therefore, the equation $|z-12|=\tfrac{5}{3}|z-8i|$ tells us that $z$ must lie on the ellipse with foci $D$ and $E$, and major axis twice as long as the segment connecting $D$ and $E$. Using the distance formula, we see that $DE=4\sqrt{10}$, and $\tfrac{1}{2}DE = 2\sqrt{10}$, so the semi-major axis of the ellipse is $2\sqrt{10}$. Since the foci are $2i$ units apart and the major axis is twice as long as the distance between the foci, the semi-minor axis of the ellipse is $\sqrt{(2\sqrt{10})^2 - 2^2} = \sqrt{396} = 6\sqrt{11}$. Since $D=(12,0)$ and $E=(0,8)$, the center of the ellipse is the midpoint of segment $DE$: $C = (\tfrac{1}{2}(12+0),\tfrac{1}{2}(0+8)) = (6,4)$. Thus, the equation of the ellipse is
\[\frac{(x-6)^2}{(2\sqrt{10})^2} + \frac{(y-4)^2}{(6\sqrt{11})^2} = 1.\]Finally, we find all points on the $y$-axis ($x=0$) that also lie on this ellipse. We obtain
\[\frac{(0-6)^2}{(2\sqrt{10})^2} + \frac{(y-4)^2}{(6\sqrt{11})^2} = 1,\]which simplifies to $\tfrac{(y-4)^2}{396} = \tfrac{9}{10}$, or $y=4\pm\sqrt{360} = 4\pm6\sqrt{10}$. Therefore, the complex numbers that satisfy the given equations are $z=\boxed{4\pm(6+8i)\sqrt{10},\,4\pm(6-8i)\sqrt{10}}$.

Because $k \leq \sqrt[3]{n_i} < k+1$, it follows that $k^3 \leq n_i
< (k+1)^3 = k^3 +3k^2 +3k +1$. Because $k$ is a divisor of $n_i$, there are $3k+4$ possible values for $n_i$, namely $k^3, k^3 +k,
\ldots, k^3 +3k^2 +3k$. Hence $3k+4 = 70$ and $k =22$. The desired maximum is $\dfrac{k^3 + 3k^2 + 3k}{k} = k^2 + 3k + 3 = \boxed{553}$.

The value $k$ must be less than or equal to the cube root of the largest possible $n_i$, because for $\lfloor\sqrt[3]{n_i}\rfloor > k$, $n_i\geq(\lfloor\sqrt[3]{n_i}\rfloor+1)^3>k^3$. Thus the largest possible $n_i$ is $k^3$, and we can construct the full list of $n_i$ by choosing 70 integers between $1$ and $k^3$ inclusive, inclusive that are equivalent to $k$ mod $k+1$ (because for $n<k^3$ and $k^3-n<k+1$ we have $\lfloor\sqrt[3]{n}\rfloor=k=\lfloor\sqrt[3]{k^3-n}\rfloor$).

The largest possible $\frac{n}{k}$ is $\frac{k^3}{k}$, and this is equal to $k^2$. Therefore we need to maximize $k^2$.

We see that $6^3 = 216$, and $7^3 = 343,$ so we are looking for a number $k$ such that $216\leq k^3 < 343$. The integer cube root of $216$ is $6$, while the integer cube root of $343$ is $7$. Thus $k$ must be $6$.

Any $n_i$ that satisfies the conditions must be an integer multiple of $6$, so we divide each $n_i$ by $6$ (and divide $k$ by $6$ as well).  Since $\frac{n_i}{k} = \frac{6n_i}{6k}$, the maximum value of $\frac{n_i}{k}$ is equal to the maximum value of $\frac{6n}{k}$.

Since $k=6$, we have $\lfloor \sqrt[3]{n}\rfloor  = 6$, so $n\ge 6^3 = 216$. We also know that $n\le 7^3-1 = 342$.

Thus, $\frac{6n}{6k} = \frac{n}{k}\leq\frac{7^3-1}{6} = \frac{342}{6} = 57.$

Therefore, the maximum possible value of $\frac{n_i}{k}$ is $\boxed{57}$.
